mum of 10000 components. 
MS14 
3 revenue streams explored 
 
Project structure 
 
WP1: Establishing of VPP hardware infrastructure at industrial partners, with reference implementa-
tion at DTU 
Leader: Joint lead by Krebs & Co and Carmo 
Partners: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT) 
 
System selection is performed in the WP1. The selected system must be sufficiently open to allow 
for automation and custom build job generation while being sufficiently rugged to allow for uncompro-
mised reliability while delivering excellent production quality.  
MS1: Machine specification and review. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D1.1 Based on typical component requirements for Krebs & Co and Carmo, a systems re-
quirement matrix is generated, which will form the basis for machine selection 
==PAGE:196==
 
 
 
 
File number: 2081-00004B 
Page 14 of 18 
F A
M
• 
D1.2 A VPP systems provider review is conducted to identify potential technology platforms 
on which AM-Farm can be based 
MS2 Procurement and establishment. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D2.1 The VPP machines are procured from the systems provider 
• 
D2.2 The VPP machines are set up and qualified. 
Success criteria for MS1,MS2: when the systems are selected based on dimensional requirements 
of parts to be manufactured, purchased and installed in the consortium facilities. 
 
 
WP2: Establishing of digital framework and job queueing system 
Leader: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT)  
Partners: Krebs & Co, Carmo 
 
The ambition is to build a unified software solution that combines job planning, queueing generation, 
execution and monitoring into one joint software interface. The digital framework requires a solution 
to ethernet enable the VPP systems if there is no such native support and to retrofit the VPP systems 
with a computer vision system to survey build jobs as they are executed. 
MS3 Digital hardware infrastructure establishment. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D3.1 The VPP systems are set up as networked devices over ethernet.  
• 
D3.2 Based on an existing 3D file slicer and job generator a plugin is built to allow for job 
generation for the commercial VPP systems 
MS4: Development of unified software solution. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D4.1 A software flow representation and graphical user interface (GUI) demonstrator is built 
and tested.  
• 
D4.2 Beta version 1 of the unified software is ready. 
• 
D4.3 Release candidate 1 of the software is ready 
Success criteria for MS3,MS4: when the initial digital process chain steps (from design to manufac-
turing) architecture are established via a centralized control. 
 
Following the digital-physical infrastructure linkage, the different steps are identified, optimized and 
generalized to the product range selected as initial pilot productions. The different modules (job plan-
ning, queueing generation, execution and monitoring) will be connected to introduce autonomous 
management of manufacturing operations. 
 
WP3: Establishing of the post processing line 
Leader: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT)  
Partners: Krebs & Co, Carmo 
 
The post processing line embody the bulk of the VPP process chain and occupies most manual labor 
in existing VPP production facilities. The steps include the washing in solvent, drying, UV and/or 
thermal post curing, support removal and polishing. In setting up the post processing line the following 
milestones and deliverables elaborate on how this will be achieved. 
MS7 Automated washing of components with integrated solvent recovery. Achieved when the follow-
ing deliverables are met: 
• 
D7.1 A solvent recovery unit is fitted to an industrial component washer and put to service at 
the VPP facility at the industrial partners. An identical unit is built for the research lab at the 
==PAGE:197==
 
 
 
 
File number: 2081-00004B 
Page 15 of 18 
F A
M
academic partner to ensure 1-1 knowledge transfer for recovery optimization of individual 
resin systems.  
• 
D7.2 The washing unit is prepared for automated build platform insertion and removal 
MS8 Geometry dictated UV post curing. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D8.1 Prototype UV post curing unit built and ready for industrial testing at industrial partners 
• 
D8.2 Refined UV post curing unit built based upon learnings from D6.1 and implemented with 
industrial partners in the AM Farm process chain 
MS9 Scarfree Support Removal and polishing. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D9.1 Primary approach for scar free support interfaces pursued 
• 
D9.2 Secondary approach to scar free support interfaces pursued 
Success criteria for MS7-MS9: when collaborative environment integrating automation within opera-
tors tasks is established. Focus is given on alleviating the risk of chemical rinsing of the fabricate, 
which cause an unwanted mixed chemical waste stream. Support structure that cradles the compo-
nent should be successfully removed.  
 
WP4: Environmental Solution Development 
Leader: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT)  
Partners: Krebs & Co, Carmo 
 
It is a primary objective to establish the AM-Farm on an environmentally conscious foundation. It is 
however expected that, as pioneers in this pursuit, that many unidentified environmental improve-
ments to the VPP process chain will be identified throughout the duration of the project. WP4 is ded-
icated to capture these improvements, test their applicability and if promise is shown, implement 
these on the process chain. The implementation will be ad hoc and thus the deliverables and mile-
stones are as follows. 
MS10: Environmental Solution Development. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D10.1 A minimum of 6 unidentified approaches to minimizing environmental footprint is iden-
tified. 
• 
D10.2 A minimum of 2 of the identified approaches are tested towards industry scale.  
MS11: Value chain optimization. Achieved when the following deliverables are met: 
• 
D11.1 Energy and value chain solutions prototyped at lab scale. 
• 
D11.2. Energy and value chain solutions integrated in the AM-farm facility 
• 
D11.3 AM-Farm target of an energy consumption of VSEC of 5 kJ/cm3 demonstrated 
 
Success criteria for MS10-MS11: when developing solution towards chemical rinsing of the fabricate, 
reduce waste stream to which there is currently no effective means to decontaminate said mixture. 
When recycling of chemical rinsing mixture and of the cross-linked resin support structure are tested 
on lab-scale.  
 
WP5: Automation and Autonomous production 
Leader: Joint lead by Krebs & Co and Carmo 
Partners: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT)  
 
Automation will in part be achieved by introducing a standard build platform interface coupling to allow 
for untroubled transfer of components along the process chain. Full computer model of the compo-
nents and their location of the build platform is known in software, the intent is to develop a universal 
method for subsequent component handling.

WP6: Commercialization 
Leader: Joint lead by Krebs & Co and Carmo 
Partners: Krebs & Co, Carmo 
 
Krebs & Co and Carmo respectively have operated VPP based AM systems as part of their prototyp-
ing services for their injection moulding customers. WP6 activities will leverage on the fact that these 
customers are acquainted with, and often enthralled by the potential of production via VPP based AM 
at intermediate scale. The work is streamed through out the WP activities following these milestones:

and Carmo to received printed parts in small batches production using hybrid version of the developed 
automated work procedures.  
 
 
WP7: Governance and project management 
Leader: DTU Civil and Mechanical Engineering (CONSTRUCT)  
Partners: Krebs & Co, Carmo 
 
Bi-weekly meetings anchored at DTU will address problems heads-up and carry out the project man-
agement. Consortium-wide status meetings will be held every six months, to which the steering com-
mittee meetings will be linked. Dissemination activities will also be included in this WP. 
Academic dissemination is lead by DTU, at which the AM research group is internationally renowned 
for their research specifically into VPP based systems. Target journals are: Journal of Additive Man-
ufacturing, CIRP Annals, and Journal of Manufacturing Engineering. Target conferences are: Solid 
Freeform Fabrication and ASPE/EUSPEN SIG meetings on AM. 
Krebs & Co and Carmo currently operate each their pilot production facility where prototypes and 
very low volume manufacturing is carried out by VPP. Furthermore, as highly skilled component 
manufacturers and injection moulders the industrial partners are in close contact with the device

Risk assessment 
Risk: Automation of washing cycle doesn’t work for ‘difficult geometries’ with enclosed features 
(WP3) 
Impact: Certain designs might impact the fully automated workflow planned within AM-Farm 
Likelihood: Moderate 
Mitigation: Optimize the thermal and UV curing of ‘difficult geometries’ to ensure that the post-process 
can eventually be fully automated  
Risk: Failure to establish all environmental elements of the AM-Farm process chain (WP4) 
Impact: Minimized green footprint of industrial production will not be realized 
Likelihood: Moderate 
Mitigation: Focus on the largest environmental impactor in the VPP process chain; the waste stream 
from solvent/cleaning and tackle this as singularly. If time permits, focus on secondary implements. 
This will ensure that the AM-Farm is more sustainable than existing VPP production setups, while 
making massive gains on the automation.  
Risk: Failure to automate the facility (WP5) 
Impact: Productivity, lack of abolishing of work environmental hazards involved with photopolymer 
handling 
Likelihood: Low to Moderate 
Mitigation: Focus on the digital framework around the VPP systems (job planner etc.) as this is the 
technology that enables automation. The physical implementation can then be executed after the 
project has ended and a profitable business has been grown.  
 
Risk: Lack of business interest (WP6) 
Impact: Failure to grow a profitable business 
Likelihood: Low to Moderate 
Mitigation: Actively pursue aid from Danish manufacturing initiatives such as MADE and Danish 
AM-HUB to ensure dissemination and communication.  
 
Risk: IPR Conflict (WP6) 
Impact: Detrimental for the project as this will hinder open collaboration 
Likelihood: Low 
Mitigation: This is mitigated before the conflict even can occur through setting up an IPR transfer 
agreement as part of the collaboration agreement if the project receives funding. This ensures that 
all partners has a clear understanding of the ownership of IPR brought into the consortium.

File number: 2081-00004B 
Page 18 of 18 
F A

Plan for data management in the project 
The data management plan will be governed by the DTU data management planning frame-
work. Every research activity at DTU is governed by a policy and a set of guidelines and proce-
dures of the retention of primary materials and data as defined by DTU Civil and Mechanical 
Engineering. The AM Farm project will as a natural part of the conduct at DTU be audited ac-
cordingly to ensure that data is handled appropriately. 
This policy ensures that valuable data are stored securely at DTU or at external repositories, and 
that the level of availability is decided. The policy also implements procedures for the secure stor-
age of data, products (e.g. experimental setup, models etc.) and their publications and for storing a 
specified level of metadata. 
Further this is a tool to help researchers in finding and using existing infrastructure, resources and 
useful tools in the most efficient way and leading them to the right support for all aspects related to 
data management. 
The policy ensures ultimately that data is handled in a compliant manner, with ethical considera-
tions and legal rules as described in the DTU Policy of the Retention of Primary Materials and Data 
and the DTU Danish Code of Conduct for Research Integrity. 
 
 
Dissemination of knowledge about the project in a societal context 
The knowledge dissemination from AM Farm is of a technical nature and is thus primarily relevant 
in scientific publications and technical/commercial papers.

SECTION 4: FIRST AID MEASURES 
 
4.1. Description of first aid measures 
 
General information 
Get medical attention if any discomfort continues. 
Inhalation 
Move the exposed person to fresh air at once.  Get medical attention if any discomfort continues. 
Ingestion 
Do not induce vomiting. If vomiting occurs, the head should be kept low so that stomach vomit doesn't enter the lungs. Get medical 
attention.  Never give liquid to an unconscious person. 
Skin contact 
Remove contaminated clothing immediately and wash skin with soap and water. Get medical attention if any discomfort continues. 
Eye contact 
Immediately flush with plenty of water for up to 15 minutes. Remove any contact lenses and open eyes wide apart. To hospital or eye 
specialist.

Inhalation. 
May cause irritation to the respiratory system. No specific health warnings noted. 
Ingestion 
There may be irritation of the throat 
Skin contact 
May cause skin irritation/eczema. 
Eye contact 
Irritating and may cause redness and pain.

Firstly, the data (difference in masses) from the ”which solvent works best” section is
statistically analysed. It is analysed using ANOVA, followed by the shapiro­Wilks test to
see if the assumption of ”normallity” (normally distributed residuals around 0, and variance
of sigma^2). This is followed by the Levene test: testing the assumption of Homogeniety
of variances. A Q­Q plot is also plotted for visuallisation of the normality assumption (also
called the ”Fat pencil” test, wherein the residuals should fall on a straight line, indicating
normally distributed residuals). The power of the dataset and post­hoc routines:Tukey's
HSD test, Bonferroni correction and Holm's method are also performed.
[] import numpy as np import scipy.stats as stats import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from statsmodels.stats.multicomp import pairwise_tukeyhsd, MultiComparison from
statsmodels.stats.power import FTestAnovaPower
# Provided data IPA = [0.523, 0.492, 0.447, 0.417, 0.529, 0.553, 0.554, 0.549, 0.545,
0.584, 0.648, 0.57, 0.6, 0.543, 0.574] TPM = [0.555, 0.559, 0.596, 0.551, 0.617, 0.53,
0.518, 0.522, 0.508, 0.518, 0.542, 0.473, 0.559, 0.52, 0.556] Anmasi = [0.542, 0.473,
0.559, 0.52, 0.556, 0.514, 0.518, 0.546, 0.546, 0.526, 0.564, 0.607, 0.585, 0.61, 0.591]
# Perform ANOVA f_value, p_value = stats.f_oneway(IPA, TPM, Anmasi) print(”F­value:”,
f_value, ”P­value:”, p_value)
# Combine all data into a single list for residual calculation all_data = np.concatenate([IPA,
TPM, Anmasi]) overall_mean = np.mean(all_data)
# Calculate residuals residuals = np.concatenate([
np.array(IPA) ­ np.mean(IPA),
np.array(TPM) ­ np.mean(TPM), np.array(Anmasi) ­ np.mean(Anmasi) ])
# Perform Shapiro­Wilk test on residuals shapiro_stat, p_normality = stats.shapiro(residuals)
print(”Shapiro­Wilk Test: Statistic =”, shapiro_stat, ”, p­value =”, p_normality)
# Perform Levene's test for homogeneity of variances levene_stat, p_homogeneity =
stats.levene(IPA, TPM, Anmasi) print(”Levene's Test: Statistic =”, levene_stat, ”, p­value
=”, p_homogeneity)
# Power calculation effect_size = np.sqrt(f_value / (len(IPA) + len(TPM) + len(Anmasi) ­ 3))
# Effect size calculation anova_power = FTestAnovaPower() power = anova_power.solve_power(effect_s
k_groups=3, nobs=len(IPA) + len(TPM) + len(Anmasi), alpha=0.05) print(”Power of the
dataset:”, power)
# Q­Q plot for Normality Check stats.probplot(residuals, dist=”norm”, plot=plt) plt.title(”Q­
Q Plot of Residuals”) plt.show()
# Prepare data for post­hoc tests group_labels = (['IPA'] * len(IPA) + ['TPM'] * len(TPM)
+ ['Anmasi'] * len(Anmasi))
all_values = np.concatenate([IPA, TPM, Anmasi])
# Tukey's HSD test tukey = pairwise_tukeyhsd(endog=all_values, groups=group_labels,
alpha=0.05) print(tukey) tukey.plot_simultaneous() plt.title(”Tukey's HSD Test”) plt.show()
# Bonferroni correction mc = MultiComparison(all_values,
group_labels) bonfer­
roni_result,
bonferroni_summary,
_ = mc.allpairtest(stats.ttest_ind,
method='bonf')

­The P­value for the F­statistic is P­val=0.83, which is above alpha=0.05, meaning we
cannot reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The solvents are the same”. Meaning that there
is not a statistically significant difference between the means of the dataset.
­The P­value for the Shapiro­Wilks test (Normallity) is P­val=0.28, which is above al­
pha=0.05, meaning we cannot reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The residuals are nor­
mally distributed”. which means the assumption is accommondated.
­The P­value for the Levene test (Homogeneity of Variances) is P­val=0.50, which is above
alpha=0.05, meaning we cannot reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The variances are
equal across all groups”. which means the assumption is accommondated.
­The power of the dataset is 0.065 (6.5%) meaning that there is a 100% ­ 6.5% = 93.5%
chance of making a Type II error, which is very high (fail to reject a false null hypothesis)

tested groups.

­The P­value for the F­statistic is P­val=4.64e^­05, which is below alpha=0.05, meaning
we can reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The methods are all the same”. Meaning that
there is a statistically significant difference between the means of the dataset. It requires
further investigation as to find which specific mean/s are the different one/ones. This will
be done using Post­Hoc methods: Tukey's HSD test, Bonferroni correction and Holm's
method
­The P­value for the Shapiro­Wilks test (Normallity) is P­val=0.67, which is above al­
pha=0.05, meaning we cannot reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The residuals are nor­
mally distributed”. which means the assumption is accommondated.
­The P­value for the Levene test (Homogeneity of Variances) is P­val=0.46, which is above
alpha=0.05, meaning we cannot reject the null hypothesis that is: ”The variances are
equal across all groups”. which means the assumption is accommondated.
­The power of the dataset is 0.79 (79%) meaning that there is a 100% ­ 79% = 21% chance
of making a Type II error, which indicates a slightly higher chance of making a type II error
(fail to reject a false null hypothesis). The power level should be above 0.8 (80%)
­The post­hoc tests: Tukey's HSD test, Bonferroni correction and Holm's method indicate
that there is a statistical significant difference between the means of: [Tukey's Test]: Spin­
ning & Static, Spinning+Ultrasonic & Static, Spinning+Ultrasonic & Stirring, Static & Stir­
ring, Static & Ultrasonics.[Bonferroni Correction]: Spinning & Static, Spinning & Stirring,
Spinning+Ultrasonic & Static. [Holm's Method]: Spinning & Static, Spinning & Stirring,
Spinning+Ultrasonic & Static, Static & Ultrasonics.

# Provided data IPA_Static_Rinse = [0.523, 0.492, 0.447, 0.417, 0.529] TPM_Static_Rinse

0.520, 0.556]
# Perform ANOVA f_value, p_value = stats.f_oneway(IPA_Static_Rinse, TPM_Static_Rinse,

# Combine all data into a single list for residual calculation all_data = np.concatenate([IPA_Static_Rinse,
TPM_Static_Rinse, ANMASI_Static_Rinse]) overall_mean = np.mean(all_data)
# Calculate residuals residuals = np.concatenate([
np.array(IPA_Static_Rinse) ­
np.mean(IPA_Static_Rinse), np.array(TPM_Static_Rinse) ­ np.mean(TPM_Static_Rinse),
np.array(ANMASI_Static_Rinse) ­ np.mean(ANMASI_Static_Rinse) ])
# Perform Shapiro­Wilk test on residuals shapiro_stat, p_normality = stats.shapiro(residuals)
print(”Shapiro­Wilk Test: Statistic =”, shapiro_stat, ”, p­value =”, p_normality)
# Perform Levene's test for homogeneity of variances levene_stat, p_homogeneity =
stats.levene(IPA_Static_Rinse, TPM_Static_Rinse, ANMASI_Static_Rinse) print(”Levene's
Test: Statistic =”, levene_stat, ”, p­value =”, p_homogeneity)
# Power calculation effect_size = np.sqrt(f_value / (len(IPA_Static_Rinse) + len(TPM_Static_Rinse)
+ len(ANMASI_Static_Rinse) ­ 3)) # Effect size calculation anova_power = FTes­

nobs=len(all_data), alpha=0.05) print(”Power of the dataset:”, power)

Q Plot of Residuals”) plt.show()

+

+

*
len(ANMASI_Static_Rinse))

# Tukey's HSD test tukey = pairwise_tukeyhsd(endog=all_values, groups=group_labels,
alpha=0.05) print(tukey) tukey.plot_simultaneous() plt.title(”Tukey's HSD Test”) plt.show()

group_labels) bonfer­

distributed residuals). The power of the dataset and post­hoc routines:Tukey's HSD test,
